     <p><b>Rutgers University</b> <span class="nowrap"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/?/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">?</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'r' in 'rye'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">r</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/?/ short 'u' in 'bud'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">?</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'t' in 'tie'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">t</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'g' in 'guy'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">?</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/?r/ 'er' in 'finger'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">?r</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'z' in 'Zion'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">z</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span>, officially <b>Rutgers, The State University of New Jersey</b>, is an American <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Doctoral_university" title="Doctoral university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> and the largest institution for <a href="/wiki/Higher_education_in_New_Jersey" title="Higher education in New Jersey">higher education in New Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. It was originally chartered as <b>Queen's College</b> in 1766. It is the eighth-oldest college in the United States and one of the nine <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Colleges" title="Colonial Colleges" class="mw-redirect">Colonial Colleges</a> founded before the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>. Rutgers was originally a <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private university</a> affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed Church</a> and admitted only male students, but evolved into a <a href="/wiki/Coeducation" title="Coeducation" class="mw-redirect">coeducational</a> <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a>. Rutgers is one of only two colonial colleges that later became public universities, the other being the <a href="/wiki/College_of_William_%26_Mary" title="College of William &amp; Mary">College of William &amp; Mary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Rutgers was designated The State University of New Jersey by acts of the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Legislature" title="New Jersey Legislature">New Jersey Legislature</a> in 1945 and 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-1956law_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1956law-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> The University consists of three campuses?the main campus in <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick,_New_Jersey" title="New Brunswick, New Jersey">New Brunswick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Piscataway_Township,_New_Jersey" title="Piscataway Township, New Jersey" class="mw-redirect">Piscataway</a>, and branch campuses in <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">Camden</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Newark" title="Rutgers?Newark">Newark campus</a> was formerly the University of Newark, which merged into the Rutgers system in 1946, and the <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Camden" title="Rutgers?Camden">Camden campus</a> was created in 1950 from the College of South Jersey and the South Jersey Law School.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university is the largest <a href="/wiki/State_university_system" title="State university system">state university</a> within New Jersey. The university offers more than 100 distinct <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_degree" title="Bachelor degree" class="mw-redirect">bachelor</a>, 100 <a href="/wiki/Masters_degree" title="Masters degree" class="mw-redirect">master</a>, and 80 <a href="/wiki/Doctoral_degree" title="Doctoral degree" class="mw-redirect">doctoral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Professional_degree" title="Professional degree" class="mw-redirect">professional degree</a> programs across 175 academic departments, 29 degree-granting schools and colleges, 16 of which offer graduate programs of study.<sup id="cite_ref-GettingToKnow_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GettingToKnow-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Rutgers is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>, a consortium of the top 62 most elite research universities in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-aau.edu_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aau.edu-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table id="toc" class="toc"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td> 
         <div id="toctitle"> 
          <h2>Contents</h2> 
         </div> 
         <ul> 
          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a> 
           <ul> 
            <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Colonial_period"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Colonial period</span></a></li>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:OldQueensRutgers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/OldQueensRutgers.jpg/220px-OldQueensRutgers.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/OldQueensRutgers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/OldQueensRutgers.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:OldQueensRutgers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Early 19th-century drawing of Old Queen's (1809), the oldest building on the Rutgers University campus in New Brunswick, New Jersey.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Rutgers_University" title="History of Rutgers University">History of Rutgers University</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period">Colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colonial period">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Two decades after the <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">College of New Jersey</a> (now Princeton University) was established in 1746 by the New Light Presbyterians, <a href="/wiki/Minister_(Christianity)" title="Minister (Christianity)">ministers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed Church</a>, seeking autonomy in ecclesiastical affairs in the American colonies, sought to establish a college to train those who wanted to become <a href="/wiki/Clergy" title="Clergy">ministers</a> within the church.<sup id="cite_ref-andthen_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-andthen-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Through several years of effort by Rev. <a href="/wiki/Theodorus_Jacobus_Frelinghuysen" title="Theodorus Jacobus Frelinghuysen">Theodorus Jacobus Frelinghuysen</a> (1691?1747) and Rev. <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Rutsen_Hardenbergh" title="Jacob Rutsen Hardenbergh">Jacob Rutsen Hardenbergh</a> (1736?1790), later the college's first president, <i>Queen's College</i> received its charter on November 10, 1766 from New Jersey's last Royal Governor, <a href="/wiki/William_Franklin" title="William Franklin">William Franklin</a> (1730?1813), the illegitimate son of Founding Father <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">Benjamin Franklin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-andthen_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-andthen-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The original charter established the college under the corporate name <i>the trustees of Queen's College, in New-Jersey</i>, named in honor of <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">King George III</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Queen-consort" title="Queen-consort" class="mw-redirect">Queen consort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_of_Mecklenburg-Strelitz" title="Charlotte of Mecklenburg-Strelitz">Charlotte of Mecklenburg-Strelitz</a> (1744?1818), and created both the college and the Queen's College Grammar School, intended to be a <a href="/wiki/University-preparatory_school" title="University-preparatory school">preparatory school</a> affiliated and governed by the college.<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The Grammar School, today the private <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Preparatory_School" title="Rutgers Preparatory School">Rutgers Preparatory School</a>, was a part of the college community until 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The location of New Brunswick was chosen over Hackensack because the New Brunswick Dutch had the support of the Anglican population as well, making the royal charter easier to obtain.</p> 
     <p>The original purpose of Queen's College was to &quot;<i>educate the youth in language, liberal, the divinity, and useful arts and sciences</i>&quot; and for the training of future ministers for the Dutch Reformed Church<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The college admitted its first students in 1771?a single sophomore and a handful of first-year students taught by a lone instructor?and granted its first degree in 1774, to <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Leydt" title="Matthew Leydt">Matthew Leydt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite the religious nature of the early college, the first classes were held at a <a href="/wiki/Tavern" title="Tavern">tavern</a> called the <i>Sign of the Red Lion.</i><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> When the Revolutionary War broke out and taverns were suspected by the British as being hotbeds of rebel activity, the college abandoned the tavern and held classes in private homes.<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_troubles_and_a_benefactor">Financial troubles and a benefactor</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Financial troubles and a benefactor">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:213px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Henryrutgers.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f0/Henryrutgers.png" width="211" height="304" class="thumbimage" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Henryrutgers.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Oil painting of Revolutionary War hero and 
        <a href="/wiki/Philanthropist" title="Philanthropist" class="mw-redirect">philanthropist</a>, Colonel 
        <a href="/wiki/Henry_Rutgers" title="Henry Rutgers">Henry Rutgers</a> (1745?1830), early benefactor and namesake of Rutgers University.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In its early years, due to a lack of funds, Queen's College was closed for two extended periods. Early trustees considered merging the college with the <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">College of New Jersey</a>, in Princeton (the measure failed by one vote) and later considered relocating to New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1808, after raising $12,000, the college was temporarily reopened and broke ground on a building of its own, affectionately called &quot;<a href="/wiki/Old_Queens" title="Old Queens">Old Queens</a>&quot;, designed by architect <a href="/wiki/John_McComb,_Jr." title="John McComb, Jr.">John McComb, Jr.</a><sup id="cite_ref-paths_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paths-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The college's third president, the Rev. <a href="/wiki/Ira_Condict" title="Ira Condict">Ira Condict</a>, laid the cornerstone on April 27, 1809. Shortly after, the <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick_Theological_Seminary" title="New Brunswick Theological Seminary">New Brunswick Theological Seminary</a>, founded in 1784, relocated from <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn,_New_York" title="Brooklyn, New York" class="mw-redirect">Brooklyn, New York</a>, to New Brunswick, and shared facilities with Queen's College (and the <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Preparatory_School" title="Rutgers Preparatory School">Queen's College Grammar School</a>, as all three institutions were then overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Church_in_America" title="Reformed Church in America">Reformed Church in America</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> During those formative years, all three institutions fit into Old Queens. In 1830, the Queen's College Grammar School moved across the street, and in 1856, the Seminary relocated to a seven-acre (28,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) tract less than one-half mile (800&nbsp;m) away.<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>After several years of closure resulting from an economic depression after the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, Queen's College reopened in 1825 and was renamed <i>Rutgers College</i> in honor of <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> hero Colonel <a href="/wiki/Henry_Rutgers" title="Henry Rutgers">Henry Rutgers</a> (1745?1830). According to the Board of Trustees, Colonel Rutgers was honored because he epitomized <a href="/wiki/Christian_values" title="Christian values">Christian values</a>. A year after the school was renamed, it received 2 donations from its namesake: a $200 bell still hanging from the cupola of Old Queen's and a $5,000 bond which placed the college on sound financial footing.<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land-grant_college">Land-grant college</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Land-grant college">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Rutgers College became the <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_college" title="Land-grant college" class="mw-redirect">land-grant college</a> of New Jersey in 1864 under the <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Land-Grant_Colleges_Act" title="Morrill Land-Grant Colleges Act" class="mw-redirect">Morrill Act of 1862</a>, resulting in the establishment of the Rutgers Scientific School, featuring departments of <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The Rutgers Scientific School would expand over the years to grow into the New Jersey Agricultural Experiment Station (1880) and divide into the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Engineering_(Rutgers_University)" title="School of Engineering (Rutgers University)">College of Engineering</a> (1914) and the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Environmental_and_Biological_Sciences_(Rutgers_University)" title="School of Environmental and Biological Sciences (Rutgers University)">College of Agriculture</a> (1921).<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Rutgers created the <a href="/wiki/Douglass_College_(Rutgers_University)" title="Douglass College (Rutgers University)" class="mw-redirect">New Jersey College for Women</a> in 1918, and the School of Education in 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> With the development of graduate education, and the continued expansion of the institution, the collection of schools became Rutgers University in 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-years_11-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Rutgers College continued as a liberal arts college within the university. Later, <a href="/wiki/School_of_Arts_and_Sciences_(Rutgers_University)" title="School of Arts and Sciences (Rutgers University)">University College</a> (1945) was founded to serve part-time, commuting students and <a href="/wiki/Livingston_College" title="Livingston College">Livingston College</a> (1969) was created by the Rutgers Trustees, ensuring that the interests of ethnically diverse New Jersey students were met.<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_University">State University</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: State University">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Rutgers was designated the State University of New Jersey by acts of the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Legislature" title="New Jersey Legislature">New Jersey Legislature</a> in 1945 and 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-1956law_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1956law-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Shortly after, the <i>University of Newark</i> (1935) was merged with Rutgers in 1946, as were the <i>College of South Jersey</i> and <i>South Jersey Law School,</i> in 1950. These two institutions became <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Newark" title="Rutgers?Newark">Rutgers?Newark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Camden" title="Rutgers?Camden">Rutgers?Camden</a>. On September 10, 1970, after much debate, the Board of Governors voted to admit women into Rutgers College.<sup id="cite_ref-sketch_10-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sketch-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-years_11-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Growth of the University was not without setbacks. In 1967 Rutgers Physics Department had a Centers of Excellence Grant from the NSF which allowed the Physics Department to hire several faculty each year and become a more prominent Institution. These faculty were to be paid by the grant for three years, but after that time any faculty hired with the Associate or Full Professor designation would become tenured. The Governor and the Chancellor forced Rutgers to lose this grant by rejecting these faculty as tenured. Not too long after this a bond issue arose that would increase financial support at Rutgers and develop Rutgers into a more prestigious University. This Bond was vetoed by the Governor, and when the Bond was turned down, the Chancellor explained that Rutgers University would never be a Princeton.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_University_event_for_admitted_students_in_basketball_stadium.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Rutgers_University_event_for_admitted_students_in_basketball_stadium.JPG/220px-Rutgers_University_event_for_admitted_students_in_basketball_stadium.JPG" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Rutgers_University_event_for_admitted_students_in_basketball_stadium.JPG/330px-Rutgers_University_event_for_admitted_students_in_basketball_stadium.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Rutgers_University_event_for_admitted_students_in_basketball_stadium.JPG/440px-Rutgers_University_event_for_admitted_students_in_basketball_stadium.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_University_event_for_admitted_students_in_basketball_stadium.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> As New Jersey's 
        <a href="/wiki/Flagship_university" title="Flagship university" class="mw-redirect">flagship university</a>, Rutgers attracts top students from around the state. Photo: admissions personnel welcome newly admitted students at the Louis Brown Athletic Center on the Livingston campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1970 the newly formed Rutgers Medical School had achieved a great deal of fame with major faculty members coming from other institutions to be part of this new enterprise. But in 1971 the Governor's Office separated Rutgers Medical School from Rutgers University and made it part of New Jersey College of Medicine and Dentistry, and many faculty left the Medical School, including the dean of the Medical School, Dr. Dewitt Stetten, who later became the Director of the National Institutes of Health. As a result of the separation of the Medical School from Rutgers University, graduate PhD programs that had been started in the medical center were lost, and students had to seek other institutions to finish their degrees.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rutgers_University_today">Rutgers University today</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Rutgers University today">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Prior to 1982, separate liberal arts faculties existed in the several &quot;<a href="/wiki/Residential_college" title="Residential college">residential colleges</a>&quot;, (Rutgers, Douglass, Livingston, University, and Cook colleges) at Rutgers?New Brunswick. In 1982, under president <a href="/wiki/Edward_J._Bloustein" title="Edward J. Bloustein">Edward J. Bloustein</a>, the faculties were centralized into one college, the Faculty of Arts and Sciences, but the residential colleges persisted for students, along with disparate standards for admission, good standing, and graduation, as well as a confusing network of bureaucracies. Finally in the fall of 2007, the residential colleges and Faculty of Arts and Sciences were merged into the new <i><a href="/wiki/School_of_Arts_and_Sciences_(Rutgers_University)" title="School of Arts and Sciences (Rutgers University)">School of Arts and Sciences</a></i> with one set of admissions criteria, curriculum and graduation requirements. Cook College changed its name to the School of Environmental and Biological Sciences and shedding the option to major in liberal arts. The merger ended the 241 year history of Rutgers College as a distinct institution.</p> 
     <p>In 2013, most of the University of Medicine and Dentistry of New Jersey was integrated with Rutgers University and, along with several existing Rutgers units, was reformed as <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Biomedical_and_Health_Sciences" title="Rutgers Biomedical and Health Sciences">Rutgers Biomedical and Health Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CHE_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHE-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> This merger reunited Rutgers Medical School (now <a href="/wiki/Robert_Wood_Johnson_Medical_School" title="Robert Wood Johnson Medical School">Robert Wood Johnson Medical School</a>) with Rutgers University.</p> 
     <p>On June 20, 2012, the outgoing president of Rutgers University, <a href="/wiki/Richard_L._McCormick" title="Richard L. McCormick" class="mw-redirect">Richard L. McCormick</a> announced that Rutgers will &quot;...integrate five acres along George Street between Seminary Place and Bishop Place into the College Avenue Campus.&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Much of this is land currently occupied by the <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick_Theological_Seminary" title="New Brunswick Theological Seminary">New Brunswick Theological Seminary</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_administration">Organization and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Organization and administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Old_Queens_Rutgers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Old_Queens_Rutgers.jpg/220px-Old_Queens_Rutgers.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Old_Queens_Rutgers.jpg/330px-Old_Queens_Rutgers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Old_Queens_Rutgers.jpg/440px-Old_Queens_Rutgers.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Old_Queens_Rutgers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Winter at Old Queens, the oldest building at Rutgers University in New Brunswick, New Jersey, built between 1809?1825. Old Queens currently houses much of the Rutgers University administration.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_president">University president</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: University president">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_presidents_of_Rutgers_University" title="List of presidents of Rutgers University">List of presidents of Rutgers University</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Twenty men have served as the president of Rutgers University, beginning with Reverend Jacob Rutsen Hardenbergh who was appointed to the office in 1785. The current, and twentieth president, is <a href="/wiki/Robert_L._Barchi" title="Robert L. Barchi">Robert L. Barchi</a> (b. 1946), a board-certified physician and neuroscientist who previously served as president of the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson_University" title="Thomas Jefferson University">Thomas Jefferson University</a> in Philadelphia and as provost of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>. Barchi was appointed on 11 April 2012 to succeed outgoing president <a href="/wiki/Richard_Levis_McCormick" title="Richard Levis McCormick">Richard L. McCormick</a> (b. 1947), and assumed the office on 1 September 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's president serves as the chief administrator overseeing the day-to-day operations of all three campuses and?in an <i>ex officio</i> capacity?a presiding officer within the University's 59-member Board of Trustees and its eleven-member Board of Governors. The university president is answerable and responsible to these boards alone, and not to any political officers or elected officials.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governing_Boards">Governing Boards</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Governing Boards">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Governance at Rutgers University rests with a <i>Board of Trustees</i> consisting currently of 59 members and a <i>Board of Governors</i> consisting of 11 members: 6 appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_Jersey" title="Governor of New Jersey">Governor of New Jersey</a> and 5 chosen by the Board of Trustees.<sup id="cite_ref-Targeted_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Targeted-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The trustees constitute chiefly an advisory body to the Board of Governors and are the fiduciary overseers of the property and assets of the University that existed before the institution became the State University of New Jersey in 1945. The initial reluctance of the trustees (still acting as a private corporate body) to cede control of certain business affairs to the state government for direction and oversight caused the state to establish the Board of Governors in 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Today, the Board of Governors maintains much of the corporate control of the University.</p> 
     <p>The members of the Board of Trustees are voted upon by different constituencies or appointed. &quot;Two faculty and two students are elected by the University Senate as nonvoting representatives. The 59 voting members are chosen in the following way as mandated by state law: 28 charter members (of whom at least three shall be women), 20 alumni members nominated by the Nominating Committee of the Board of Trustees, and five public members appointed by the governor of the state with confirmation by the New Jersey State Senate. The six members of the Board of Governors appointed by the governor also serve as members of the Board of Trustees. Of the 28 charter seats, three are reserved for students with full voting rights.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Affiliations">Affiliations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Affiliations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Middle_States_Association_of_Colleges_and_Schools" title="Middle States Association of Colleges and Schools">Middle States Association of Colleges and Schools</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Committee_on_Institutional_Cooperation" title="Committee on Institutional Cooperation">Committee on Institutional Cooperation</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Universities_Research_Association" title="Universities Research Association">Universities Research Association</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Association_of_Public_and_Land-grant_Universities" title="Association of Public and Land-grant Universities">Association of Public and Land-grant Universities</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/American_Athletic_Conference" title="American Athletic Conference">American Athletic Conference</a> (through June 30, 2014)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> (beginning July 1, 2014)</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Rutgers University has three campuses across the state of <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, with its largest campus located mainly in the City of <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick,_New_Jersey" title="New Brunswick, New Jersey">New Brunswick</a> and adjacent <a href="/wiki/Piscataway,_New_Jersey" title="Piscataway, New Jersey">Piscataway</a> Township, and two smaller campuses in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">Camden</a>. These campuses comprise 27 degree-granting schools and colleges, offering undergraduate, graduate and professional levels of study. The university is centrally administered from New Brunswick, although Chancellors at the <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Newark" title="Rutgers?Newark">Newark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Camden" title="Rutgers?Camden">Camden</a> campuses hold significant autonomy for some academic issues. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20071223155641/http://ur.rutgers.edu/styleguide/pnames.shtml#acronyms">Rutgers Fact Book</a></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Brunswick_-_Piscataway_Campus">New Brunswick - Piscataway Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: New Brunswick - Piscataway Campus">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93New_Brunswick" title="Rutgers?New Brunswick">Rutgers?New Brunswick</a>
     </div>

        </div> Bishop House has served various academic purposes on the Rutgers University campus since 1925.

     </div> 
     <p>The <i>New Brunswick-Piscataway Campus</i> (or <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93New_Brunswick" title="Rutgers?New Brunswick">Rutgers?New Brunswick</a>) is the largest campus of Rutgers; it is the site of the original Rutgers College. It is spread across six municipalities in <a href="/wiki/Middlesex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Middlesex County, New Jersey">Middlesex County, New Jersey</a>, chiefly in the City of New Brunswick and Piscataway Township. It is composed of five smaller campuses, and a few buildings in downtown New Brunswick. The original and historic <i>College Avenue</i> campus is adjacent to downtown New Brunswick, and includes the seat of the University, Old Queens. On the other side of the city, <i>Douglass Campus</i> and <i>Cook Campus</i> are adjacent and intertwined with each other, and are often referred to collectively as the <i>Cook/Douglass Campus.</i> Cook Campus has extensive farms and woods that reach into North Brunswick and East Brunswick Townships. Separated by the Raritan river are <a href="/wiki/Busch_Campus" title="Busch Campus" class="mw-redirect">Busch Campus</a>, in Piscataway, and <i>Livingston Campus</i>, also mainly in Piscataway but including remote sections of land extending into Edison Township and the Borough of Highland Park. The <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Campus_Buses" title="Rutgers Campus Buses">Rutgers Campus Buses</a> transports students between the various campuses.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of the Fall 2010, the New Brunswick-Piscataway campuses include 19 undergraduate, graduate and professional schools, including the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Arts_and_Sciences_(Rutgers_University)" title="School of Arts and Sciences (Rutgers University)">School of Arts and Sciences</a>, the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Communication_and_Information_(Rutgers_University)" title="School of Communication and Information (Rutgers University)">School of Communication and Information</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Edward_J._Bloustein_School_of_Planning_and_Public_Policy" title="Edward J. Bloustein School of Planning and Public Policy">Edward J. Bloustein School of Planning and Public Policy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Engineering_(Rutgers_University)" title="School of Engineering (Rutgers University)">School of Engineering</a>, the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Environmental_and_Biological_Sciences_(Rutgers_University)" title="School of Environmental and Biological Sciences (Rutgers University)">School of Environmental and Biological Sciences</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Mario_School_of_Pharmacy" title="Ernest Mario School of Pharmacy">Ernest Mario School of Pharmacy</a>, the Graduate School, the Graduate School of Applied and Professional Psychology, the Graduate School of Education, the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Management_and_Labor_Relations" title="School of Management and Labor Relations">School of Management and Labor Relations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mason_Gross_School_of_the_Arts" title="Mason Gross School of the Arts">Mason Gross School of the Arts</a>, the College of Nursing, the <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Business_School" title="Rutgers Business School" class="mw-redirect">Rutgers Business School</a> and the School of Social Work. As of 2012, 31,593 undergraduates and 8,841 graduate students (total 40,434) are enrolled at the New Brunswick-Piscataway campus.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The New Brunswick- Piscataway campus will include a Business School that is currently being built on the Livingston Campus in order to accommodate the rising interest of students wanting to receive a business degree.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rutgers.E2.80.93Newark">Rutgers?Newark</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rutgers?Newark">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Newark" title="Rutgers?Newark">Rutgers?Newark</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <i>Newark Campus</i> (or <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Newark" title="Rutgers?Newark">Rutgers?Newark</a>), consists of 8 undergraduate, graduate and professional schools, including: Newark College of Arts and Sciences, University College, School of Criminal Justice, Graduate School, College of Nursing, <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University_School_of_Public_Affairs_and_Administration" title="Rutgers University School of Public Affairs and Administration">School of Public Affairs and Administration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Business_School" title="Rutgers Business School" class="mw-redirect">Rutgers Business School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_School_of_Law_-_Newark" title="Rutgers School of Law - Newark" class="mw-redirect">Rutgers School of Law - Newark</a>. As of 2012, 7,666 undergraduates and 4,345 graduate students (total 12,011 are enrolled at the Newark campus.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rutgers.E2.80.93Camden">Rutgers?Camden</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Rutgers?Camden">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Camden" title="Rutgers?Camden">Rutgers?Camden</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <i>Camden Campus</i> (or <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Camden" title="Rutgers?Camden">Rutgers?Camden</a>) consists of five undergraduate, graduate and professional schools, including: Camden College of Arts and Sciences, University College, Graduate School, <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_School_of_Business_%E2%80%93_Camden" title="Rutgers School of Business ? Camden">Rutgers School of Business ? Camden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_School_of_Law_-_Camden" title="Rutgers School of Law - Camden" class="mw-redirect">Rutgers School of Law - Camden</a>. As of 2012, 4,708 undergraduates and 1,635 graduate students (total 6,343) are enrolled at the Camden campus.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Rutgers has offers classes at several off-campus in affiliation with community colleges and other state colleges throughout New Jersey.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NewJerseyHall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/NewJerseyHall.jpg/220px-NewJerseyHall.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/NewJerseyHall.jpg/330px-NewJerseyHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/NewJerseyHall.jpg/440px-NewJerseyHall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NewJerseyHall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> New Jersey Hall on the New Brunswick College Avenue Campus was the home of the Agricultural Experiment Station, Biology and Chemistry faculty. It now houses the university's Department of Economics.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Profile">Profile</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Profile">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Established in 1766, Rutgers, The State University of New Jersey is one of the nine <a href="/wiki/Colonial_colleges" title="Colonial colleges" class="mw-redirect">colonial chartered colleges</a> established before the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>. In 1864, the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Legislature" title="New Jersey Legislature">New Jersey Legislature</a> selected Rutgers as New Jersey's sole <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_university" title="Land-grant university">land-grant college</a> which expanded the school's offerings in the fields of practical agriculture, science, military science and engineering. The state legislature designated Rutgers to be New Jersey's <a href="/wiki/State_university" title="State university" class="mw-redirect">state university</a> by acts passed in 1945 and 1956.. It is the only university in the United States able to boast all three designations.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The university offers more than 100 distinct bachelor, 100 master, and 80 doctoral and professional degree programs across 175 academic departments, 29 degree-granting schools and colleges, 16 of which offer graduate programs of study.</p> 
     <p>Rutgers is accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Middle_States_Commission_on_Higher_Education" title="Middle States Commission on Higher Education" class="mw-redirect">Commission on Higher Education</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_States_Association_of_Colleges_and_Schools" title="Middle States Association of Colleges and Schools">Middle States Association of Colleges and Schools</a> (1921), and in 1989, became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>, an organization of the 62 leading research universities in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-aau.edu_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aau.edu-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93New_Brunswick" title="Rutgers?New Brunswick">Rutgers?New Brunswick</a> is classified by the <a href="/wiki/The_Carnegie_Foundation_for_the_Advancement_of_Teaching" title="The Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching" class="mw-redirect">Carnegie Foundation</a> as &quot;RU/VH&quot;, which stands for Research Intensive University, Very High research activity.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Newark" title="Rutgers?Newark">Rutgers?Newark</a> is classified by the same organization as &quot;RU/H&quot;, meaning Research Intensive University, High research activity and <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Camden" title="Rutgers?Camden">Rutgers?Camden</a> is given the classification of &quot;Master's M&quot;, signifying the university's inclusion in the Master's Colleges and Universities category as a medium-sized institution.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Alexander_Library.jpg/220px-Alexander_Library.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Alexander_Library.jpg/330px-Alexander_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Alexander_Library.jpg/440px-Alexander_Library.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Archibald S. Alexander Library is the main library at Rutgers University.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_University_Art_Library.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Rutgers_University_Art_Library.JPG/220px-Rutgers_University_Art_Library.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Rutgers_University_Art_Library.JPG/330px-Rutgers_University_Art_Library.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Rutgers_University_Art_Library.JPG/440px-Rutgers_University_Art_Library.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_University_Art_Library.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> An art library on the College Avenue campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Rutgers University library system consists of 26 libraries and centers located on the University's three campuses, housing a collection of over 10.5 million holdings, including 3,656,283 volumes, 4,600,902 microforms, 2,535,892 documents, and subscriptions to 91,078 periodicals and other electronic resources, and ranking among the nation's top research libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_Library_Association" title="American Library Association">American Library Association</a> ranks the Rutgers University Library system as the 44th largest library in the United States in terms of volumes held.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Archibald_S._Alexander" title="Archibald S. Alexander">Archibald S. Alexander</a> Library</i>, in <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick,_New_Jersey" title="New Brunswick, New Jersey">New Brunswick</a>, is the oldest and the largest library of the University.<sup id="cite_ref-AlexCollection_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlexCollection-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> It houses several million volumes focusing on an extensive <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social science</a> collection.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It mainly supports the sort of research done in the School of Arts and Sciences, the Edward J. Bloustein School of Planning &amp; Public Policy, the Graduate School of Education, the Graduate School of Social Work, and the School of Communication and Information. Alexander Library also maintains a large collection of government documents, which contains United States, New Jersey, foreign, and international government publications.<sup id="cite_ref-AlexCollection_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlexCollection-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>Library of Science and Medicine</i> on the Busch Campus in <a href="/wiki/Piscataway,_New_Jersey" title="Piscataway, New Jersey">Piscataway</a> houses the University's collection in <a href="/wiki/Behavioral_science" title="Behavioral science" class="mw-redirect">behavioral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biological</a>, <a href="/wiki/Earth_science" title="Earth science">earth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_science" title="Pharmaceutical science" class="mw-redirect">pharmaceutical sciences</a> and <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>. The LSM also serves as a designated depository library for government publication regarding science, and owns a U.S. patent collection and patent search facility.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> It was officially established as the Library of Science and Medicine in July 1964 although the beginning of the development of a library for science started in 1962. The current character of the LSM is a university science library also serving a medical school.<sup id="cite_ref-LSMhistory_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSMhistory-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> On the New Brunswick-Piscataway campus, in addition to Alexander Library, many individual disciplines have their own libraries, including alcohol studies, <a href="/wiki/Art_history" title="Art history">art history</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">Chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Math" title="Math" class="mw-redirect">Mathematical</a> studies, <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">Music</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">Physics</a>. <i>Special Collections and University Archives</i> houses the Sinclair New Jersey Collection, manuscript collection, and rare book collection, as well as the University <a href="/wiki/Archives" title="Archives" class="mw-redirect">Archives</a>. Although located in the Alexander Library building, <a href="/wiki/Special_Collections" title="Special Collections" class="mw-redirect">Special Collections</a> and University Archives actually comprises a distinct unit unto itself. Also located within the Alexander Library is the <i>East Asian Library</i> which holds a sizable collection of Chinese, Japanese and Korean monographs and periodicals. In <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Newark" title="Rutgers?Newark">Newark</a>, the <i>John Cotton Dana Library</i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Jazz_Studies" title="Institute of Jazz Studies">Institute of Jazz Studies</a></i> (located within the Dana Library), and the <i><a href="/wiki/Paul_Robeson" title="Paul Robeson">Paul Robeson</a> Library</i> in <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Camden" title="Rutgers?Camden">Camden</a>, serve their respective campuses with a broad collection of volumes. Individual items and collections within the Libraries can be identified using the <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Rutgers_Information_System" title="Integrated Rutgers Information System">Rutgers University Library Catalog</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_collections">Museums and collections</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Museums and collections">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Zimmerli_Art_Museum_at_Rutgers_University.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Zimmerli_Art_Museum_at_Rutgers_University.jpg/220px-Zimmerli_Art_Museum_at_Rutgers_University.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Zimmerli_Art_Museum_at_Rutgers_University.jpg/330px-Zimmerli_Art_Museum_at_Rutgers_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Zimmerli_Art_Museum_at_Rutgers_University.jpg/440px-Zimmerli_Art_Museum_at_Rutgers_University.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Zimmerli_Art_Museum_at_Rutgers_University.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Jane Voorhees Zimmerli Art Museum on Hamilton Street in New Brunswick
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Rutgers oversees several museums and collections that are open to the public.</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Zimmerli_Art_Museum_at_Rutgers_University" title="Zimmerli Art Museum at Rutgers University">Jane Voorhees Zimmerli Art Museum</a>, on the College Avenue Campus maintains a collection of over 50,000 works of art, focusing on Russian and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> art, French 19th-century art and <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_America" title="United States of America" class="mw-redirect">American</a> 19th- and 20th-century art with a concentration on early-20th-century and contemporary prints.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University_Geology_Museum" title="Rutgers University Geology Museum">Rutgers University Geology Museum</a> in Geology Hall features exhibits on <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropology</a>, with an emphasis on the natural history of New Jersey. The largest exhibits include a <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaur</a> <a href="/wiki/Fossil_trackway" title="Fossil trackway">trackway</a> from <a href="/wiki/Towaco,_New_Jersey" title="Towaco, New Jersey">Towaco, New Jersey</a>; a <a href="/wiki/Mastodon" title="Mastodon">mastodon</a> from <a href="/wiki/Salem_County,_New_Jersey" title="Salem County, New Jersey">Salem County</a>; and a <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ptolemaic_Egypt" title="History of Ptolemaic Egypt" class="mw-redirect">Ptolomaic</a> era <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egyptian</a> <a href="/wiki/Mummy" title="Mummy">mummy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Museum_of_Agriculture" title="New Jersey Museum of Agriculture">New Jersey Museum of Agriculture</a> on Cook Campus, houses an extensive collection of agricultural, scientific and household tools that spans 350 years of New Jersey's history. The bulk of the collection rests on the 8,000-item Wabun C. Krueger Collection of Agricultural, Household, and Scientific Artifacts, and over 30,000 glass negatives and historic <a href="/wiki/Photography" title="Photography">photographs</a>. This has since been closed.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><i>Rutgers Gardens</i>, which features 50 <a href="/wiki/Acre" title="Acre">acres</a> (20&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">ha</a>) of horticultural, display, and <a href="/wiki/Botanical_gardens" title="Botanical gardens" class="mw-redirect">botanical gardens</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">arboretums</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Rutgers' facilities across the three campuses include a golf course, <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Gardens" title="Rutgers Gardens">botanical gardens</a>, working agricultural, horse, dairy, and <a href="/wiki/Student_Sustainable_Farm_at_Rutgers" title="Student Sustainable Farm at Rutgers">sustainable farms</a>, a creamery, an <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Ecological_Preserve" title="Rutgers Ecological Preserve">ecological preserve</a> with multiple use trails, television and radio studios, theaters, museums, athletic facilities, helipads, a <a href="/wiki/Makerspace" title="Makerspace" class="mw-redirect">makerspace</a>, and more.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions_and_financial_aid">Admissions and financial aid</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Admissions and financial aid">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> considers the New Brunswick campus of Rutgers University to be a &quot;more selective&quot; school in terms of the rigor of its admissions processes.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> For 2006, 56% of undergraduate applicants were accepted, and average <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> scores of enrolling students ranged from 530?630 on the critical reading section, 560?670 for the mathematics section, and 530-640 for the writing section.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As a state university, Rutgers charges two separate rates for tuition and fees depending on whether an enrolled student is a resident of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._State" title="U.S. State" class="mw-redirect">State</a> of New Jersey (in-state) or not (out-of-state). The <i>Office of Institutional Research and Academic Planning</i> estimates that costs in-state student of attending Rutgers would amount to $25,566 for an undergraduate living on-campus and $30,069 for a graduate student. For an out-of-state student, the costs rise to $38,228 and $39,069 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> As of the 2012-2013 academic school year, the cost of attendance for in-state students is $13,073, $26,393 for out-of-state students and $11,412 for Room and Board.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the 2010-2011 academic year, undergraduate students at Rutgers, through a combination of federal (53.5%), state (23.6%), university (18.1%), and private (4.8%) scholarship, loans, and grants, received $492,260,845 of <a href="/wiki/Financial_aid_(educational_expenses)" title="Financial aid (educational expenses)" class="mw-redirect">financial aid</a>. 81.4% of all undergraduates, or 34,473 students, received some form of financial aid. During the same period, graduate students, through a combination of federal (61.9%), state (1.8%), university (34.5%), and private (1.9%) scholarship, loans, and grants received $182,384,256 of financial aid. 81.5% of all graduate students, or 11,852 students received some form of financial aid.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a>]</span></h3>
