     <p>Rutgers was ranked 38th nationwide and 54th worldwide in the 2008 <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> by the Institute of Higher Education at <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiao_Tong_University" title="Shanghai Jiao Tong University">Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a>'s 2006 rankings, Rutgers ranks 53rd in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Top American Research Universities</i> an annual statistical report by The Center at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida">University of Florida</a> ranks Rutgers 39th.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2009 <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranking of American national universities, Rutgers is ranked 64th.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2003, the Wall Street Journal conducted a study of the undergraduate institutions that most frequently feed students placements at elite professional and graduate programs, such as <a href="/wiki/Yale" title="Yale" class="mw-redirect">Yale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harvard" title="Harvard" class="mw-redirect">Harvard</a>; Rutgers was ranked 20th in the rankings they compiled for state universities.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> On a side note, Forbes ranked Rutgers as being the 20th best public university in the United States for &quot;getting rich&quot;, as judged by its students' median salaries upon graduation.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Eleven of Rutgers' graduate departments are ranked by the National Research Council in the top 25 among all universities: <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">Philosophy</a> (2nd), <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">Geology</a> Ranked 9th Nationally based on <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">NSF</a> funding 9th, <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">Geography</a> (13th), <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">Statistics</a> (17th), <a href="/wiki/English_studies" title="English studies">English</a> (17th), <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">Mathematics</a> (19th), <a href="/wiki/Art_History" title="Art History" class="mw-redirect">Art History</a> (20th), <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">Physics</a> (20th), <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">History</a> (20th) <a href="/wiki/Comparative_Literature" title="Comparative Literature" class="mw-redirect">Comparative Literature</a> (22nd), <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> (22nd), and <a href="/wiki/Materials_Science" title="Materials Science" class="mw-redirect">Materials Science Engineering</a> (25th).<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Business_School" title="Rutgers Business School" class="mw-redirect">Rutgers Business School</a> is ranked 39th in the <i><a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Journal" title="Wall Street Journal" class="mw-redirect">Wall Street Journal</a>'s</i> Ranking of Top Business Schools.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The Master of Quantitative Finance (M.S.Q.F.) program at <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Business_School" title="Rutgers Business School" class="mw-redirect">Rutgers Business School</a> and Master of Mathematical Finance (M.S.M.F) program at the department of Mathematics, is ranked 7th in the United States, behind <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a> and ahead of <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Philosophy Department ranked first in 2002?04 tied with <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a> and Princeton University, and second in 2004?06 (NYU was first, Princeton 3rd, Oxford 4th) in the <a href="/wiki/Philosophical_Gourmet" title="Philosophical Gourmet" class="mw-redirect">Philosophical Gourmet</a>'s biennial report on <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">Philosophy</a> programs in the English-speaking world.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_Univeristy_Clock.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Rutgers_Univeristy_Clock.jpg/220px-Rutgers_Univeristy_Clock.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Rutgers_Univeristy_Clock.jpg/330px-Rutgers_Univeristy_Clock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Rutgers_Univeristy_Clock.jpg/440px-Rutgers_Univeristy_Clock.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_Univeristy_Clock.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Rutgers Quad Clock on College Avenue.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Division of Global Affairs (DGA)<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://dga.rutgers.edu/">[3]</a> Ph.D. program at Rutgers University-Newark was ranked fifth in the nation in the Benchmarking Academic Excellence survey of Top Universities in Social and Behavioral Sciences Disciplines in the combined category of International Affairs and Development for 2006-07.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to U.S. News &amp; World Report, Rutgers ranks in the top 25 among all US universities for the following subjects: Food Science (2nd), <a href="/wiki/Library_Science" title="Library Science" class="mw-redirect">Library Science</a> (6th), <a href="/wiki/Drama" title="Drama">Drama</a>/<a href="/wiki/Theater" title="Theater" class="mw-redirect">Theater</a> (12th), <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">Mathematics</a> (16th), <a href="/wiki/English_studies" title="English studies">English</a> (18th), <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">History</a> (19th, with the subspecialty of African-American History ranked 4th and Women's History ranked 1st), <a href="/wiki/Applied_Mathematics" title="Applied Mathematics" class="mw-redirect">Applied Mathematics</a> (21st) and <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">Physics</a> (24th).<sup id="cite_ref-Targeted_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Targeted-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Also in the 2006 U.S. News &amp; World Report ranking of Computer Science Ph.D. programs, Rutgers was ranked 29th.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On September 13, 2010, the Wall Street Journal ranked Rutgers University #21 in schools whose graduates are top-rated by recruiters.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On June 28, 2012 the New Jersey state legislature passed the New Jersey Medical and Health Sciences Education Restructuring Act that will dissolve the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Medicine_and_Dentistry_of_New_Jersey" title="University of Medicine and Dentistry of New Jersey">University of Medicine and Dentistry of New Jersey</a> and merge most of its schools, including <a href="/wiki/Robert_Wood_Johnson_Medical_School" title="Robert Wood Johnson Medical School">Robert Wood Johnson Medical School</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Medical_School" title="New Jersey Medical School">New Jersey Medical School</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Dental_School" title="New Jersey Dental School" class="mw-redirect">New Jersey Dental School</a>, with Rutgers University forming a new Rutgers School of Biomedical and Health Sciences by July 1, 2013. Members of the Rutgers Board of Governors estimated that the takeover of UMDNJ could &quot;elevate Rutgers? status to among the top 25 most elite research universities in America.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Selman_Waksman_NYWTS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Selman_Waksman_NYWTS.jpg/220px-Selman_Waksman_NYWTS.jpg" width="220" height="270" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Selman_Waksman_NYWTS.jpg/330px-Selman_Waksman_NYWTS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Selman_Waksman_NYWTS.jpg/440px-Selman_Waksman_NYWTS.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Selman_Waksman_NYWTS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Prof. 
        <a href="/wiki/Selman_A._Waksman" title="Selman A. Waksman" class="mw-redirect">Selman A. Waksman</a> (B.Sc. 1915), who was awarded the Nobel Prize in Medicine for developing 22 antibiotics?most notably Streptomycin?in his laboratory at Rutgers University.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Rutgers is home to the Rutgers University Center for <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_Science" title="Cognitive Science" class="mw-redirect">Cognitive Science</a>, also known as <a href="/w/index.php?title=RUCCS&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="RUCCS (page does not exist)">RUCCS</a>. Researchers in <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguistics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropology</a> combine resources to advance the study of the mind at this state of the art institution.</p> 
     <p>It was at Rutgers that <a href="/wiki/Selman_Waksman" title="Selman Waksman">Selman Waksman</a> (1888?1973) discovered several <a href="/wiki/Antibiotic" title="Antibiotic" class="mw-redirect">antibiotics</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Actinomycin" title="Actinomycin">actinomycin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clavacin" title="Clavacin" class="mw-redirect">clavacin</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Streptothricin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Streptothricin (page does not exist)">streptothricin</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Grisein&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Grisein (page does not exist)">grisein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neomycin" title="Neomycin">neomycin</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fradicin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fradicin (page does not exist)">fradicin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Candicidin" title="Candicidin">candicidin</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Candidin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Candidin (page does not exist)">candidin</a>, and others. Waksman, along with graduate student <a href="/wiki/Albert_Schatz_(scientist)" title="Albert Schatz (scientist)">Albert Schatz</a> (1920?2005), discovered <a href="/wiki/Streptomycin" title="Streptomycin">streptomycin</a>?a versatile antibiotic that was to be the first applied to cure <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>. For this discovery, Waksman received the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize for Medicine" class="mw-redirect">Nobel Prize for Medicine</a> in 1952.</p> 
     <p>Rutgers developed water-soluble sustained release polymers, <a href="/wiki/Polyploidy" title="Polyploidy" class="mw-redirect">tetraploids</a>, robotic hands, <a href="/wiki/Artificial_insemination" title="Artificial insemination">artificial bovine insemination</a>, and the ceramic tiles for the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_thermal_protection_system" title="Space Shuttle thermal protection system">heat shield</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a>. In health related field, Rutgers has the Environmental &amp; Occupational Health Science Institute (EOHSI).</p> 
     <p>Rutgers is also home to the RCSB Protein Data bank,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> 'an information portal to Biological Macromolecular Structures' cohosted with the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Supercomputer_Center" title="San Diego Supercomputer Center">San Diego Supercomputer Center</a>. This database is the authoritative research tool for bioinformaticists using protein primary, secondary and tertiary structures world wide.'</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Great_Swamp_Greenhouse_photos_Rutgers_Tomato.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Great_Swamp_Greenhouse_photos_Rutgers_Tomato.JPG/220px-Great_Swamp_Greenhouse_photos_Rutgers_Tomato.JPG" width="220" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Great_Swamp_Greenhouse_photos_Rutgers_Tomato.JPG/330px-Great_Swamp_Greenhouse_photos_Rutgers_Tomato.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Great_Swamp_Greenhouse_photos_Rutgers_Tomato.JPG/440px-Great_Swamp_Greenhouse_photos_Rutgers_Tomato.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Great_Swamp_Greenhouse_photos_Rutgers_Tomato.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <i>Rutgers Tomato</i> growing at a New Jersey greenhouse.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Rutgers is home to the Rutgers Cooperative Research &amp; Extension office, which is run by the Agricultural and Experiment Station with the support of local government. The institution provides research &amp; education to the local farming and agro industrial community in 19 of the 21 counties of the state and educational outreach programs offered through the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Agricultural_Experiment_Station_Office_of_Continuing_Professional_Education" title="New Jersey Agricultural Experiment Station Office of Continuing Professional Education">New Jersey Agricultural Experiment Station Office of Continuing Professional Education</a>.</p> 
     <p>Rutgers University Cell and DNA Repository (RUCDR) is the largest university based repository in the world and has received awards worth more than $57.8 million from the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> (NIH). One will fund genetic studies of mental disorders and the other will support investigations into the causes of digestive, liver and kidney diseases, and diabetes.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> RUCDR activities will enable gene discovery leading to diagnoses, treatments and, eventually, cures for these diseases. RUCDR assists researchers throughout the world by providing the highest quality biomaterials, technical consultation, and logistical support.</p> 
     <p>Rutgers?Camden is home to the nation's PhD granting Department of Childhood Studies. This department, in conjunction with the Center for Children and Childhood Studies, also on the Camden campus, conducts interdisciplinary research which combines methodologies and research practices of sociology, psychology, literature, anthropology and other disciplines into the study of childhoods internationally.</p> 
     <p>Rutgers is home to several <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> IGERT fellowships that support interdisciplinary scientific research at the graduate-level. Highly selective fellowships are available in the following areas: Perceptual Science, <a href="/wiki/Stem_Cell" title="Stem Cell" class="mw-redirect">Stem Cell</a> Science and Engineering, <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">Nanotechnology</a> for Clean Energy, Renewable and Sustainable Fuels Solutions, and Nanopharmaceutical Engineering.</p> 
     <p>Rutgers also maintains the Office of Research Alliances<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> that focuses on working with companies to increase engagement with the university's faculty members, staff and extensive resources on the three campuses.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residential_life">Residential life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Residential life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Vorhees_Chapel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Vorhees_Chapel.jpg/220px-Vorhees_Chapel.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Vorhees_Chapel.jpg/330px-Vorhees_Chapel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Vorhees_Chapel.jpg/440px-Vorhees_Chapel.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Vorhees_Chapel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Voorhees Chapel is a notable landmark on the Douglass campus at Rutgers. Douglass was originally founded as an all-women's college in 1918, but now houses co-ed dormitories.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Rutgers University offers a variety of housing options. On the <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick,_New_Jersey" title="New Brunswick, New Jersey">New Brunswick</a>-Piscataway campus, students are given the option of on-campus housing in both traditional <a href="/wiki/Dorm" title="Dorm" class="mw-redirect">dorms</a> or apartments. Freshman students, however, are allowed only a dorm, while upperclassmen have a wider array of on-campus housing choices, like apartments. Despite some overcrowding, most students seeking on-campus housing will be accommodated with a space, yet in 2008/2009 students were placed in a nearby hotel. Many Rutgers students opt to rent apartments or houses off-campus within the city of New Brunswick. Similar setups are to be found in Rutgers?Newark and Rutgers?Camden, however a substantial portion of the students on those campuses commute and/or are enrolled on a part-time basis.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Demarest_Hall_front.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Demarest_Hall_front.JPG/220px-Demarest_Hall_front.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Demarest_Hall_front.JPG/330px-Demarest_Hall_front.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Demarest_Hall_front.JPG/440px-Demarest_Hall_front.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Demarest_Hall_front.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Demarest_Hall" title="Demarest Hall">Demarest Hall</a> dormitory
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Rutgers University's three campuses are in the culturally-diverse, redeveloping urban areas (<a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">Camden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick,_New_Jersey" title="New Brunswick, New Jersey">New Brunswick</a>) with convenient access to New York City and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> by either <a href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">automobile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> or <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Transit" title="New Jersey Transit">New Jersey Transit</a>. <a href="/wiki/US_News_%26_World_Report" title="US News &amp; World Report" class="mw-redirect">US News &amp; World Report</a> ranked <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Newark" title="Rutgers?Newark">Rutgers?Newark</a> the most diverse university campus in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Because the area of Rutgers' New Brunswick-Piscataway campus?which is composed of several constituent colleges and professional schools?is sprawled across six <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipalities</a>, the individual campuses are connected by an inter-campus <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">bus</a> system. The <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Buses" title="Rutgers Buses" class="mw-redirect">Rutgers bus system</a> is the second largest bus service in New Jersey, and one of the largest in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_and_emergency_services">Security and emergency services</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Security and emergency services">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Services provided by the university include <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University_Police_Department" title="Rutgers University Police Department">Rutgers Police</a>, Emergency Medical Services, an emergency management office, <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Buses" title="Rutgers Buses" class="mw-redirect">bus and shuttle service</a>, inter- and intra-campus mail, and occupational and environmental health and safety.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations_and_activities">Student organizations and activities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Student organizations and activities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University_student_organizations" title="Rutgers University student organizations">Rutgers University student organizations</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University_Greek_organizations" title="Rutgers University Greek organizations">Rutgers University Greek organizations</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Rutgers University has a student government which controls funding to student groups. The student government is made up of campus councils and professional school councils. Those councils then send representatives to the student assembly as well as the university senate. An example of these campus councils is the University College Council, which represents adult, part-time, and military veteran students.</p> 
     <p>Rutgers hosts over 700 <a href="/wiki/Student_organization" title="Student organization" class="mw-redirect">student organizations</a>, covering a wide range of interests. Among the first student groups was the first <a href="/wiki/College_newspaper" title="College newspaper" class="mw-redirect">college newspaper</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_America" title="United States of America" class="mw-redirect">United States of America</a>. <i>The Political Intelligencer and New Jersey Adviser</i> began publication at Queen's College in 1783, and ceased operation in 1785.<sup id="cite_ref-years_11-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Continuing this tradition is the university's current college newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Targum" title="The Daily Targum">The Daily Targum</a></i>, established in 1869, which is the second-oldest college newspaper currently published in the United States, after <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dartmouth" title="The Dartmouth">The Dartmouth</a></i> (1843). Both poet <a href="/wiki/Joyce_Kilmer" title="Joyce Kilmer">Joyce Kilmer</a> and economist <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a> served as editors. Also included are <i><a href="/wiki/The_Medium_(Rutgers)" title="The Medium (Rutgers)">The Medium</a></i>, Rutgers Entertainment Weekly, <i><a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Centurion" title="Rutgers Centurion" class="mw-redirect">Rutgers Centurion</a></i>, a conservative newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University_Glee_Club" title="Rutgers University Glee Club">Rutgers University Glee Club</a></i>, a male <a href="/wiki/Choral" title="Choral" class="mw-redirect">choral</a> singing group established in 1872 (among the oldest in the country), as well as the <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University_Debate_Union" title="Rutgers University Debate Union">Rutgers University Debate Union</a>. More recently there has been increased national exposure among Rutgers a cappella groups as they have routinely placed well in the <a href="/wiki/International_Championship_of_Collegiate_A_Cappella" title="International Championship of Collegiate A Cappella">International Championship of Collegiate A Cappella</a>, including 2010 when <a href="/wiki/The_OrphanSporks" title="The OrphanSporks">The OrphanSporks</a> placed second in the semifinals.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Governed by the <i>Rutgers University Student Assembly</i> and funded by student fees, students can organize groups for practically any political ideology or issue, ethnic or religious affiliation, academic subject, activity, or hobby.</p> 
     <p>Rutgers University is home to chapters of many Greek organizations, and a significant percentage of the undergraduate student body is active in Greek life. Several <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternities and sororities</a> maintain houses for their chapters in the area of Union Street (known familiarly as &quot;Frat Row&quot;) in <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick,_New_Jersey" title="New Brunswick, New Jersey">New Brunswick</a>, within blocks of Rutgers' College Avenue Campus. Chapters of <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Psi" title="Zeta Psi">Zeta Psi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delta_Phi" title="Delta Phi">Delta Phi</a> organized at Rutgers as early as 1845. The Alpha Rho chapter of <a href="/wiki/Chi_Psi" title="Chi Psi">Chi Psi</a> Fraternity, founded at Rutgers College in 1879, was the first fraternity at Rutgers to own a fraternity house, or &quot;Lodge&quot;, purchased in 1887. The fraternity today still owns and occupies the same property at 114 College Avenue. Today, there are over 50 fraternities and sororities on the New Brunswick-Piscataway campus, ranging from traditional to historically <a href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American" class="mw-redirect">African-American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">Multicultural</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a> interest organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The New Brunswick campus of Rutgers University has a chapter of the only active co-ed Pre-medical Fraternity, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Delta_Epsilon" title="Phi Delta Epsilon">Phi Delta Epsilon</a>, as of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Greek organizations are governed by the <i>Office of Fraternity and Sorority Affairs</i>. Twelve organizations maintain chapters in New Brunswick without sanction by the University's administration.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_University_Busch_campus_walkway_and_quadrangle_and_buildings.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Rutgers_University_Busch_campus_walkway_and_quadrangle_and_buildings.JPG/220px-Rutgers_University_Busch_campus_walkway_and_quadrangle_and_buildings.JPG" width="220" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Rutgers_University_Busch_campus_walkway_and_quadrangle_and_buildings.JPG/330px-Rutgers_University_Busch_campus_walkway_and_quadrangle_and_buildings.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Rutgers_University_Busch_campus_walkway_and_quadrangle_and_buildings.JPG/440px-Rutgers_University_Busch_campus_walkway_and_quadrangle_and_buildings.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_University_Busch_campus_walkway_and_quadrangle_and_buildings.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Several of the campuses are relatively new; the Busch campus (shown) was built within the last few decades and the Livingston campus is being expanded with new dormitories and facilities.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In the late 19th century, the University banned fraternities because of their unusual hazing practices. This caused them to go underground as secret societies. It also sparked the interest of some students to create their own societies. <a href="/wiki/Cap_and_Skull" title="Cap and Skull">Cap and Skull</a> was founded at Rutgers before the turn of the 20th century.</p> 
     <p>Today, Rutgers is well known for four of its vocal ensembles: Voorhees Choir (the university's women's ensemble), Kirkpatrick Choir (the university's most selective coed ensemble), Glee Club (the university's most esteemed male ensemble), and University Choir (a larger mixed choir).</p> 
     <p>In 2011, The Iota Psi chapter of <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a> raised a national Greek record of $167,000 for the Children?s Miracle Network with the help of seven sororities: <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Chi_Omega" title="Alpha Chi Omega">Alpha Chi Omega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Gamma" title="Delta Gamma">Delta Gamma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamma_Phi_Beta" title="Gamma Phi Beta">Gamma Phi Beta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Sigma_Sigma" title="Phi Sigma Sigma">Phi Sigma Sigma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Delta_Tau" title="Sigma Delta Tau">Sigma Delta Tau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Kappa" title="Sigma Kappa">Sigma Kappa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Tau_Alpha" title="Zeta Tau Alpha">Zeta Tau Alpha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p><i>(Note: The <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Camden" title="Rutgers?Camden">Rutgers?Camden</a> athletic teams are called the <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Camden#Athletics" title="Rutgers?Camden">Scarlet Raptors</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Newark" title="Rutgers?Newark">Rutgers?Newark</a> athletic teams are called the <a href="/wiki/Rutgers%E2%80%93Newark_Scarlet_Raiders" title="Rutgers?Newark Scarlet Raiders" class="mw-redirect">Scarlet Raiders</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_(color)#School_colors" title="Scarlet (color)">Scarlet</a> Raiders and the Scarlet Raptors both compete within NCAA <a href="/wiki/Division_III_(NCAA)" title="Division III (NCAA)">Division III</a>.)</i></p> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Scarlet_Knights" title="Rutgers Scarlet Knights">Rutgers Scarlet Knights</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_college_athletic_programs_in_New_Jersey,_USA#Division_I" title="List of college athletic programs in New Jersey, USA" class="mw-redirect">List of college athletic programs in New Jersey, USA#Division I</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Rutgers was among the first American institutions to engage in intercollegiate athletics, and participated in a small circle of schools that included <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> and long-time rival, <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a> (then called <i>The College of New Jersey</i>). The four schools met at the Fifth Avenue Hotel in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> on October 19, 1873 to establish a set of rules governing their intercollegiate competition, and particularly to codify the new game of <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">football</a>. Though invited, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a> chose not to attend.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> In the early years of intercollegiate athletics, the circle of schools that participated in these athletic events were located solely in the American Northeast. However, by the turn of the 20th century, colleges and universities across the United States began to participate.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_Rowing_Men%27s_Varsity_Eight.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/e7/Rutgers_Rowing_Men%27s_Varsity_Eight.png" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_Rowing_Men%27s_Varsity_Eight.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Rutgers Men's Varsity Eight rowing on the Raritain River.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1864, rowing became the first organized sport at Rutgers. Six mile races were held on the Raritan River among six-oared boats. In 1870, Rutgers held its first intercollegiate competition, against the Lawrence Scientific School of Harvard, the then top-ranked amateur crew of the time. Since the start in 1864, Rutgers has built a strong crew program consisting of heavyweight and lightweight men. Women's crew was added to the program in 1974. Financial support of the Men's crew program was discontinued by the university in 2006, though the Crew continues to compete (funded entirely by Alumni and private support) at a high level in the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Association_of_Rowing_Colleges" title="Eastern Association of Rowing Colleges">Eastern Association of Rowing Colleges</a> conference. The first intercollegiate athletic event at Rutgers was a baseball game on May 2, 1866 against Princeton in which they suffered a 40-2 loss.<sup id="cite_ref-years_11-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Rutgers University is often referred to as <i>The Birthplace of College Football</i> as the first <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">intercollegiate football</a> <a href="/wiki/1869_college_football_season#First_football_game_ever_played" title="1869 college football season">game was held</a> on College Field between Rutgers and Princeton on November 6, 1869 in <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick,_New_Jersey" title="New Brunswick, New Jersey">New Brunswick, New Jersey</a> on a plot of ground where the present-day <a href="/wiki/College_Avenue_Gymnasium" title="College Avenue Gymnasium">College Avenue Gymnasium</a> now stands. Rutgers won the game, with a score of 6 runs to Princeton's 4.<sup id="cite_ref-years_11-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-years-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tradition_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tradition-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Parke_H._Davis" title="Parke H. Davis">Parke H. Davis</a>, the 1869 Rutgers football team shared the national title with Princeton.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> (This game is believed to have been closer to soccer than to modern American football.)<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:1882RutgersFootballTeam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/1882RutgersFootballTeam.jpg/220px-1882RutgersFootballTeam.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b9/1882RutgersFootballTeam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b9/1882RutgersFootballTeam.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:1882RutgersFootballTeam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Rutgers College football team in 1882
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Since 1866, Rutgers remained unaffiliated with any formal athletic conference and was classified as &quot;independent&quot;. From 1946 to 1951, the university was a member of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Middle_Three_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Middle Three Conference (page does not exist)">Middle Three Conference</a>, and from 1958 to 1961, was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Atlantic_Conferences" title="Middle Atlantic Conferences">Middle Atlantic Conference</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nationalchamps_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalchamps-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1978, Rutgers became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_10" title="Atlantic 10" class="mw-redirect">Atlantic 10</a> conference. In 1991, it joined the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979?2013)">Big East Conference</a> for football. All sports programs at Rutgers subsequently became affiliated with the Big East in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The first intercollegiate competition in <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_(sport)" title="Ultimate (sport)">Ultimate Frisbee</a> (now called simply &quot;Ultimate&quot;) was held between students from Rutgers and <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton</a> on November 6, 1972 to mark the one hundred third anniversary of the first intercollegiate football game. Rutgers won 29?27.<sup id="cite_ref-Frisbee_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frisbee-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The Rutgers Men's Basketball Team was among the &quot;Final Four&quot; and ended the 1976 season ranked fourth in the United States, after an 86?70 loss against the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a> in the semifinals, and a 106?92 loss against <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a> in the consolation round of the <a href="/wiki/1976_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="1976 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">1976 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:High_Point_Solutions_Stadium-Rutgers_University.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/High_Point_Solutions_Stadium-Rutgers_University.jpg/220px-High_Point_Solutions_Stadium-Rutgers_University.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/High_Point_Solutions_Stadium-Rutgers_University.jpg/330px-High_Point_Solutions_Stadium-Rutgers_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/High_Point_Solutions_Stadium-Rutgers_University.jpg/440px-High_Point_Solutions_Stadium-Rutgers_University.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:High_Point_Solutions_Stadium-Rutgers_University.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> High Point Solutions Stadium is home to Scarlet Knights football.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Rutgers is a member of the <a href="/wiki/American_Athletic_Conference" title="American Athletic Conference">American Athletic Conference</a>, a collegiate athletic conference consisting of 10 colleges and universities from the East Coast and <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwestern</a> regions of the United States. The American Athletic Conference is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Bowl_Championship_Series" title="Bowl Championship Series">Bowl Championship Series</a>. Rutgers currently fields 27 intercollegiate sports programs and is a <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> school as sanctioned by the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a>. Rutgers fields thirty teams in NCAA Division I sanctioned sports, including <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">Football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">Baseball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sport_rowing" title="Sport rowing" class="mw-redirect">Crew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">Cross Country</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fencing_(sport)" title="Fencing (sport)" class="mw-redirect">Fencing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Field_Hockey" title="Field Hockey" class="mw-redirect">Field Hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">Golf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">Gymnastics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">Lacrosse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer" class="mw-redirect">Soccer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">Softball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">Tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Track_and_Field" title="Track and Field" class="mw-redirect">Track and Field</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">Swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diving" title="Diving">Diving</a>, <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_wrestling" title="Collegiate wrestling">Wrestling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">Volleyball</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Scarlet Knights have won five Big East Conference tournament titles: men's <a href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer" class="mw-redirect">soccer</a> (1997), men's <a href="/wiki/Track_%26_field" title="Track &amp; field" class="mw-redirect">track &amp; field</a> (2005), <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> (2000, 2007), <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_basketball" title="Women's basketball">women's basketball</a> (2007). Several other teams have won regular season titles but failed to win the conference's championship tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-Big_East_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Big_East-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Most recently, the Rutgers Scarlet Knights' football team has achieved success on the gridiron after several years of losing seasons, being invited to the <a href="/wiki/Insight_Bowl" title="Insight Bowl" class="mw-redirect">Insight Bowl</a> on December 27, 2005 in which they lost 45 to 40 against <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> This was Rutgers' first bowl appearance since the December 16, 1978 loss against Arizona State, 34?18, at the <a href="/wiki/Garden_State_Bowl" title="Garden State Bowl">Garden State Bowl</a>. The 2006 football season also saw Rutgers being ranked within the Top 25 teams in major college football polls. After the November 9, 2006 victory over the #3 ranked, undefeated <a href="/wiki/University_of_Louisville" title="University of Louisville">Louisville Cardinals</a>, Rutgers jumped up to seventh in the <a href="/wiki/AP_Poll" title="AP Poll">AP Poll</a>, eighth in the <a href="/wiki/USA_Today_Coaches_Poll" title="USA Today Coaches Poll" class="mw-redirect">USA Today/Coaches poll</a>, seventh in the <a href="/wiki/Harris_Interactive_College_Football_Poll" title="Harris Interactive College Football Poll">Harris Interactive Poll</a>, and sixth in the <a href="/wiki/Bowl_Championship_Series" title="Bowl Championship Series">Bowl Championship Series</a> rankings. These were Rutgers' highest rankings in the football polls since they were ranked fifteenth in 1961. Rutgers ended the season 11?2 after winning the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Texas_Bowl" title="Texas Bowl" class="mw-redirect">Texas Bowl</a> on December 28, 2006, defeating the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_State_Wildcats" title="Kansas State Wildcats">Wildcats</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kansas_State_University" title="Kansas State University">Kansas State University</a> by a score of 37?10 and finishing the season ranked twelfth in the final <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> poll of sportswriters, the team's highest season-ending ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Under Head Coach <a href="/wiki/C._Vivian_Stringer" title="C. Vivian Stringer">C. Vivian Stringer</a>, the Women's Basketball program is among the elite programs in the country as they remain consistently ranked in the Top 25, consistently making the NCAA Women's Championship Tournament, and sometimes winning the Big East regular season championship. In 2006-2007, Rutgers won their first ever Big East Conference Tournament Championship. The program has been highly competitive since its inception, winning the 1982 AIAW National Championship, reaching the 2000 Final Four, and reaching the Final Four and national championship game in 2007.</p> 
     <p>Rutgers maintains athletic rivalries with other collegiate institutions. The university has historic rivalries with <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> (formerly <i>King's College</i>), <a href="/wiki/Lafayette_College" title="Lafayette College">Lafayette College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_University" title="Lehigh University">Lehigh University</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a> originating from the early days of college football. While they maintain this rivalry in other sports, neither of them have met in football since 1980. Rutgers has a basketball rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Seton_Hall_University" title="Seton Hall University">Seton Hall University</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> and has developed a growing three-way rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Connecticut" title="University of Connecticut">University of Connecticut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University" title="Syracuse University">Syracuse University</a>, both fellow Big East Conference members.</p> 
     <p>In the fall of 2007, six Rutgers New Brunswick/Piscataway's NCAA Division I sports were discontinued by the University, including men's swimming and diving, men's heavyweight and lightweight crew, men's tennis, and men's and women's fencing. Some continued as club teams, while some were disbanded completely. The University claims this change was due to budget cuts, while others claim it was a politically motivated move designed to protest state's funding changes.</p> 
     <p>In November 2012, Rutgers became the latest school to leave the Big East. Syracuse and Pittsburgh have decided to enter the Atlantic Coast Conference, while West Virginia entered the Big 12 conference, taking effect as of the 2012-2013 season. Rutgers decided to leave the Big East for the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>, effective July 1, 2014. Rutgers will surpass <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_University" title="Pennsylvania State University">Penn State</a> as the Big Ten's easternmost school.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: People">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Rutgers_University_people" title="List of Rutgers University people">List of Rutgers University people</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty">Faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Faculty">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_University_New_Brunswick_NJT_train_station.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Rutgers_University_New_Brunswick_NJT_train_station.JPG/220px-Rutgers_University_New_Brunswick_NJT_train_station.JPG" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Rutgers_University_New_Brunswick_NJT_train_station.JPG/330px-Rutgers_University_New_Brunswick_NJT_train_station.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Rutgers_University_New_Brunswick_NJT_train_station.JPG/440px-Rutgers_University_New_Brunswick_NJT_train_station.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Rutgers_University_New_Brunswick_NJT_train_station.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A 
        <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Transit" title="New Jersey Transit">New Jersey Transit</a> train station is centrally located on the Rutgers campus which enables travel along the northeast corridor to cities such as 
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" title="Philadelphia, Pennsylvania" class="mw-redirect">Philadelphia</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>For the 2011?2012 academic year. Rutgers University had 2,937 full-time and part-time academic faculty members.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Among Rutgers notable current and former professors are <a href="/wiki/Alan_Prince" title="Alan Prince">Alan Prince</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Fodor" title="Jerry Fodor">Jerry Fodor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Baker_(linguist)" title="Mark Baker (linguist)">Mark Baker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Leslie" title="Alan Leslie" class="mw-redirect">Alan Leslie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rochel_Gelman" title="Rochel Gelman">Rochel Gelman</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Ciardi" title="John Ciardi">John Ciardi</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Hammell_Cook" title="George Hammell Cook">George Hammell Cook</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michael_Curtis_(professor)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Michael Curtis (professor) (page does not exist)">Michael Curtis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Ellison" title="Ralph Ellison">Ralph Ellison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Fussell" title="Paul Fussell">Paul Fussell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Trivers" title="Robert Trivers">Robert Trivers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Fergusson" title="Francis Fergusson">Francis Fergusson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Bader_Ginsburg" title="Ruth Bader Ginsburg">Ruth Bader Ginsburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mason_W._Gross" title="Mason W. Gross" class="mw-redirect">Mason W. Gross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Khachiyan" title="Leonid Khachiyan">Leonid Khachiyan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Lesk" title="Mike Lesk">Michael Lesk</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Levering_Lewis" title="David Levering Lewis">David Levering Lewis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roy_Lichtenstein" title="Roy Lichtenstein">Roy Lichtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilson_Carey_McWilliams" title="Wilson Carey McWilliams">Wilson Carey McWilliams</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Segal_(artist)" title="George Segal (artist)">George Segal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Endre_Szemer%C3%A9di" title="Endre Szemer&eacute;di">Endre Szemer&eacute;di</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunnell%27s_theorem" title="Tunnell's theorem">Jerrold Tunnell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Selman_Waksman" title="Selman Waksman">Selman Waksman</a>. During his 20 year tenure at Rutgers, <a href="/wiki/David_Levering_Lewis" title="David Levering Lewis">David Levering Lewis</a> (born 1936), a professor in the Department of History was twice awarded the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize for Biography or Autobiography</a> (1994 and 2001) for both volumes of his <a href="/wiki/Biography" title="Biography">biography</a> of <a href="/wiki/W._E._B._Du_Bois" title="W. E. B. Du Bois">W. E. B. Du Bois</a> (1868?1963) and was also the winner of the <a href="/wiki/Bancroft_Prize" title="Bancroft Prize">Bancroft</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Parkman_Prize&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Parkman Prize (page does not exist)">Parkman prizes</a>.</p> 
     <p>Five <a href="/wiki/Nobel_prizes_by_university_affiliation" title="Nobel prizes by university affiliation" class="mw-redirect">Nobel laureates</a> have been affiliated with Rutgers as either <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(teaching_staff)" title="Faculty (teaching staff)" class="mw-redirect">faculty</a> or students (<a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toni_Morrison" title="Toni Morrison">Toni Morrison</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_A._Morse" title="David A. Morse">David A. Morse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Rohrer" title="Heinrich Rohrer">Heinrich Rohrer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Selman_Waksman" title="Selman Waksman">Selman Waksman</a>).</p> 
     <p>Many members of the faculty at Rutgers have achieved top honors in their disciplines, including <a href="/wiki/Michael_R._Douglas" title="Michael R. Douglas">Michael R. Douglas</a>, a prominent <a href="/wiki/String_theory" title="String theory">string theorist</a> and the director of the New High Energy Theory Center and winner of the <a href="/wiki/Sackler_Prize" title="Sackler Prize">Sackler Prize</a> in theoretical physics in 2000. <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Fodor" title="Jerry Fodor">Jerry Fodor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zenon_Pylyshyn" title="Zenon Pylyshyn">Zenon Pylyshyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Stich" title="Stephen Stich">Stephen Stich</a> were awarded the <a href="/wiki/Jean_Nicod_Prize" title="Jean Nicod Prize">Jean Nicod Prize</a> in <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_science" title="Cognitive science">cognitive science</a>.</p> 
     <p>Furthermore, Rutgers ranks among the top three public AAU institutions in the overall percentage of women faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-BLP_sources" style=""> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image"> 
         <div style="width: 52px;">
          <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f4/Ambox_content.png" width="40" height="40" />
         </div> </td> 
        <td class="mbox-text" style=""><span class="mbox-text-span">This <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Biographies_of_living_persons" title="Wikipedia:Biographies of living persons">section of a biographical article</a> <b>needs additional <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help by adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources" class="mw-redirect">reliable sources</a>. Contentious material about living persons that is unsourced or poorly sourced <b>must be removed immediately</b>, especially if potentially <a href="/wiki/Defamation" title="Defamation">libelous</a> or harmful.</span> <small><i>(May 2012)</i></small> </span></td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>There have been over 335,000 graduates of Rutgers University.<sup id="cite_ref-GettingToKnow_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GettingToKnow-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Many alumni remain active through <a href="/wiki/Alumni_association" title="Alumni association">alumni associations</a>?including the Rutgers Alumni Association founded in 1831?annual Reunions and Homecomings, and other events. Rutgers has graduated two Nobel Laureates: <a href="/wiki/Selman_A._Waksman" title="Selman A. Waksman" class="mw-redirect">Selman A. Waksman</a> (A.B. 1915) in Medicine and <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a> (A.B. 1932) in Economics.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Alumni awarded the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> include <a href="/wiki/Michael_Shaara" title="Michael Shaara">Michael Shaara</a> (A.B. 1951), author of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Killer_Angels" title="The Killer Angels">The Killer Angels</a></i>, journalist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richard_Aregood&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Richard Aregood (page does not exist)">Richard Aregood</a> (B.A. 1965), <a href="/wiki/Roy_Franklin_Nichols" title="Roy Franklin Nichols">Roy Franklin Nichols</a> (A.B. 1918), and <a href="/wiki/Junot_D%C3%ADaz" title="Junot D&iacute;az">Junot D&iacute;az</a>.</p> 
     <p>Alumni of Rutgers have had a considerable impact in the arts, including modern sculptors <a href="/wiki/Paul_Robeson" title="Paul Robeson">Paul Robeson</a> (1919), <a href="/wiki/George_Segal_(artist)" title="George Segal (artist)">George Segal (artist)</a> (M.A. 1963) and <a href="/wiki/Alice_Aycock" title="Alice Aycock">Alice Aycock</a> (B.A. 1968). Many notable buildings in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Copley_Plaza_Hotel" title="Copley Plaza Hotel" class="mw-redirect">Copley Plaza Hotel</a>), and New York City including the <a href="/wiki/The_Dakota" title="The Dakota">The Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Hotel" title="Plaza Hotel">Plaza Hotel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Waldorf-Astoria" title="Waldorf-Astoria" class="mw-redirect">Waldorf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waldorf-Astoria" title="Waldorf-Astoria" class="mw-redirect">Astoria</a> Hotels (demolished in 1929 to make way for the <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">Empire State Building</a>) as well as several of the oldest buildings on the Rutgers University campus in New Brunswick, were designed by architect <a href="/wiki/Henry_J._Hardenburgh" title="Henry J. Hardenburgh" class="mw-redirect">Henry Janeway Hardenburgh</a> (A.B. 1871). Poet <a href="/wiki/Joyce_Kilmer" title="Joyce Kilmer">Joyce Kilmer</a> (Class of 1908), attended Rutgers for two years before transferring to <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a>, was famous for his poem <a href="/wiki/Trees_(poem)" title="Trees (poem)">&quot;Trees&quot;</a> and later died in World War I, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Pinsky" title="Robert Pinsky">Robert Pinsky</a> (B.A. 1962), was appointed <a href="/wiki/Poet_Laureate_Consultant_in_Poetry_to_the_Library_of_Congress" title="Poet Laureate Consultant in Poetry to the Library of Congress" class="mw-redirect">Poet Laureate Consultant in Poetry to the Library of Congress</a> in 1997. Filmmaker and critic <a href="/wiki/Wheeler_Winston_Dixon" title="Wheeler Winston Dixon">Wheeler Winston Dixon</a> (Ph.D. 1982) has written more than twenty five books on film history, theory and criticism, and his collected films are housed at <a href="/wiki/The_Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="The Museum of Modern Art" class="mw-redirect">The Museum of Modern Art</a> in New York City.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Milton_Friedman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Portrait_of_Milton_Friedman.jpg/170px-Portrait_of_Milton_Friedman.jpg" width="170" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Portrait_of_Milton_Friedman.jpg/255px-Portrait_of_Milton_Friedman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Portrait_of_Milton_Friedman.jpg/340px-Portrait_of_Milton_Friedman.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Milton_Friedman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Economist Milton Friedman
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Many Rutgers graduates have gone on to careers in public service, including former <a href="/wiki/U.S._Secretary_of_State" title="U.S. Secretary of State" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Secretary of State</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senator" title="United States Senator" class="mw-redirect">Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/Frederick_T._Frelinghuysen" title="Frederick T. Frelinghuysen" class="mw-redirect">Frederick T. Frelinghuysen</a> (A.B. 1836), former <a href="/wiki/U.S._Secretary_of_Energy" title="U.S. Secretary of Energy" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Secretary of Energy</a> <a href="/wiki/Hazel_O%27Leary" title="Hazel O'Leary" class="mw-redirect">Hazel O'Leary</a> (J.D. 19??), former <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> director <a href="/wiki/Louis_Freeh" title="Louis Freeh">Louis Freeh</a> (B.A. 1971), <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President of the United States</a> <a href="/wiki/Garret_A._Hobart" title="Garret A. Hobart" class="mw-redirect">Garret A. Hobart</a> (A.B. 1863), and former Representative and Senator <a href="/wiki/Clifford_P._Case" title="Clifford P. Case">Clifford P. Case</a> (A.B. 1925). Among the first students enrolled at Rutgers (when it was <i>Queen's College</i>), <a href="/wiki/Simeon_DeWitt" title="Simeon DeWitt" class="mw-redirect">Simeon DeWitt</a> (A.B. 1776) became the Surveyor-General for the Continental Army (1776?1783) during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolution</a> and classmate <a href="/wiki/James_Schureman" title="James Schureman">James Schureman</a> (A.B. 1775), served in the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">Continental Congress</a> and as a United States Senator. Seven Rutgers graduates have served as <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_Jersey" title="Governor of New Jersey">Governor of New Jersey</a>: <a href="/wiki/Charles_C._Stratton" title="Charles C. Stratton">Charles C. Stratton</a> (A.B. 1814), <a href="/wiki/William_A._Newell" title="William A. Newell">William A. Newell</a> (A.B. 1836; A.M. 1839), <a href="/wiki/George_C._Ludlow" title="George C. Ludlow">George C. Ludlow</a> (A.B. 1850, A.M. 1850), <a href="/wiki/Foster_M._Voorhees" title="Foster M. Voorhees" class="mw-redirect">Foster M. Voorhees</a> (A.B. 1876, A.M. 1879), <a href="/wiki/A._Harry_Moore" title="A. Harry Moore">A. Harry Moore</a> (J.D. 1922), <a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Hughes" title="Richard J. Hughes">Richard Hughes</a> (J.D. 1931), and <a href="/wiki/James_J._Florio" title="James J. Florio" class="mw-redirect">James J. Florio</a> (J.D. 1967). Alumnus <a href="/wiki/Joseph_P._Bradley" title="Joseph P. Bradley">Joseph P. Bradley</a> (A.B. 1836) was an Associate Justice of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> (1870?1891) and cast the tie-breaking vote on the bipartisan commission that decided the contested <a href="/wiki/1876_U.S._presidential_election" title="1876 U.S. presidential election" class="mw-redirect">American presidential election in 1876</a>.</p> 
     <p>Alumni have founded or headed businesses, including <a href="/wiki/Leonor_F._Loree" title="Leonor F. Loree">Leonor F. Loree</a> (A.B. 1877), President of the Pennsylvania Railroad, <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Marcus" title="Bernard Marcus">Bernard Marcus</a> (B.S. 1951), founder of <a href="/wiki/Home_Depot" title="Home Depot" class="mw-redirect">Home Depot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Mario" title="Ernest Mario">Ernest Mario</a> (B.S. 1961), former Chief Executive Officer of <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Duncan_McMillan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Duncan McMillan (page does not exist)">Duncan McMillan</a> (B.S. 1966), co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg L.P.</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barry_Schuler" title="Barry Schuler">Barry Schuler</a> (B.A. 1976), former Chairman and CEO of <a href="/wiki/AOL" title="AOL">AmericaOnline (AOL)</a>. Marc Milecofsky, aka <a href="/wiki/Marc_Ecko" title="Marc Ecko">Marc Ecko</a>, founded the clothing brand <a href="/wiki/Eck%C5%8D" title="Eck?" class="mw-redirect">Eck?</a> in 1993 and launched a special, limited edition collection<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> that specifically pays homage to the Scarlet Knights,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Mary Baglivo (B.A. 1979), Chairman and CEO of the Americas, Saatchi &amp; Saatchi, and <a href="/wiki/Michael_H._Fleischner" title="Michael H. Fleischner">Michael H. Fleischner</a>, founder of MarketingScoop.com.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RayRice27.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/RayRice27.jpg/170px-RayRice27.jpg" width="170" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/RayRice27.jpg/255px-RayRice27.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/RayRice27.jpg/340px-RayRice27.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RayRice27.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Rutgers alumnus 
        <a href="/wiki/Ray_Rice" title="Ray Rice">Ray Rice</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Graduates of Rutgers have gone on to make advances in medicine, mathematics and science, most notably Nobel Laureate <a href="/wiki/Selman_A._Waksman" title="Selman A. Waksman" class="mw-redirect">Selman A. Waksman</a> (B.Sc. 1915), but also including Peter C. Schultz (B.S. 1967), co-inventor of <a href="/wiki/Fiber_optics" title="Fiber optics" class="mw-redirect">fiber optics</a>, geneticist <a href="/wiki/Stanley_N._Cohen" title="Stanley N. Cohen" class="mw-redirect">Stanley N. Cohen</a> (B.Sc. 1956) who pioneered in the field of <a href="/wiki/Gene_splicing" title="Gene splicing" class="mw-redirect">gene splicing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Gluck" title="Louis Gluck">Louis Gluck</a> (B.S. 1930) the &quot;father of <a href="/wiki/Neonatology" title="Neonatology">neonatology</a>&quot;, and computer pioneer <a href="/wiki/Nathan_M._Newmark" title="Nathan M. Newmark">Nathan M. Newmark</a> (B.S. 1948) who won the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a>.</p> 
     <p>Rutgers alumni have entertained Americans for generations, including actors <a href="/wiki/Paul_Robeson" title="Paul Robeson">Paul Robeson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avery_Brooks" title="Avery Brooks">Avery Brooks</a> (B.A. 1973), <a href="/wiki/James_Gandolfini" title="James Gandolfini">James Gandolfini</a> (B.A. 1983), <a href="/wiki/Ozzie_Nelson" title="Ozzie Nelson">Oswald &quot;Ozzie&quot; Nelson</a> (B.A. 1927), <a href="/wiki/Kristin_Davis" title="Kristin Davis">Kristin Davis</a> (B.F.A. 1987), and <a href="/wiki/Calista_Flockhart" title="Calista Flockhart">Calista Flockhart</a> (B.F.A. 1988), <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Morales" title="Natalie Morales">Natalie Morales</a> (B.A. Journalism &amp; Latin American Studies) American news anchor for NBC's &quot;Today Show&quot;., adult film stars <a href="/wiki/Asia_Carrera" title="Asia Carrera">Asia Carrera</a> (B.A. 1996) and <a href="/wiki/Joanna_Angel" title="Joanna Angel">Joanna Angel</a> (B.A. 2002), and restaurateur <a href="/wiki/Mario_Batali" title="Mario Batali">Mario Batali</a> (B.A. 1982). A <a href="/wiki/Springfield_Township,_Union_County,_New_Jersey" title="Springfield Township, Union County, New Jersey">Springfield, New Jersey</a> band, <a href="/wiki/Midtown_(band)" title="Midtown (band)">Midtown</a>, was also formed by three Rutgers graduates.</p> 
     <p>In athletics, graduates of Rutgers include <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> managers <a href="/wiki/Eric_Young_(baseball)" title="Eric Young (baseball)">Eric Young</a> (B.A 1992) and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Torborg" title="Jeff Torborg">Jeff Torborg</a> (B.A. 1963); <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Jordan_(basketball)" title="Eddie Jordan (basketball)">Eddie Jordan</a> (B.A. 1977), former NBA head coach; <a href="/wiki/Sonny_Werblin" title="Sonny Werblin">Sonny Werblin</a> (A.B. 1932), former owner of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a>; and <a href="/wiki/David_Stern" title="David Stern">David Stern</a> (B.A. 1963), Commissioner of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>. Alumni in the National Football League include <a href="/wiki/Ray_Rice" title="Ray Rice">Ray Rice</a> (<a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Ravens" title="Baltimore Ravens">Baltimore Ravens</a>), <a href="/wiki/Brian_Leonard" title="Brian Leonard">Brian Leonard</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bengals" title="Cincinnati Bengals">Bengals</a>), <a href="/wiki/Shaun_O%27Hara" title="Shaun O'Hara">Shaun O'Hara</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a>), <a href="/wiki/L.J._Smith" title="L.J. Smith" class="mw-redirect">L.J. Smith</a> (<a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Eagles" title="Philadelphia Eagles">Philadelphia Eagles</a>), <a href="/wiki/Clark_Harris" title="Clark Harris">Clark Harris</a> (<a href="/wiki/Houston_Texans" title="Houston Texans">Houston Texans</a>), <a href="/wiki/Nate_Jones_(American_football)" title="Nate Jones (American football)">Nate Jones</a> (<a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a>), <a href="/wiki/Eric_Foster" title="Eric Foster">Eric Foster</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Indianapolis Colts</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Zuttah" title="Jeremy Zuttah">Jeremy Zuttah</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Buccaneers" title="Tampa Bay Buccaneers">Tampa Bay Buccaneers</a>), <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Davis_(offensive_tackle,_born_1989)" title="Anthony Davis (offensive tackle, born 1989)">Anthony Davis</a> (<a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jason_McCourty" title="Jason McCourty">Jason McCourty</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Titans" title="Tennessee Titans">Tennessee Titans</a>), <a href="/wiki/Devin_McCourty" title="Devin McCourty">Devin McCourty</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a>), <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Sosa" title="Pedro Sosa">Pedro Sosa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Sanu" title="Mohamed Sanu">Mohamed Sanu</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bengals" title="Cincinnati Bengals">Cincinnati Bengals</a>).</p> 
     <p>Fictitious alumni include <a href="/wiki/Mr._Magoo" title="Mr. Magoo">Quincy Magoo</a> (degree unknown, 1903), a lovable cartoon character from the 1950s and 1960s, was among the proudest of Rutgers' &quot;Loyal Sons.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The band <a href="/wiki/Looking_Glass_(band)" title="Looking Glass (band)">Looking Glass</a>, who are famous for their 1972 hit &quot;<a href="/wiki/Brandy_(You%27re_a_Fine_Girl)" title="Brandy (You're a Fine Girl)">Brandy (You're a Fine Girl)</a>&quot;, formed at Rutgers. They were active from 1969-1974.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutgers_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: References">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p><b>Notes</b></p> 
     <div class="reflist references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;"> 
      <ol class="references">

       <li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note: Of the nine colonial colleges, seven (Harvard, Yale, Pennsylvania, Princeton, Columbia, Brown and Dartmouth) remained private, and of the two remaining, William and Mary was taken over by the Commonwealth of Virginia and reincorporated as a public institution in 1888, and Rutgers became the State University of <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> by acts of the state legislature in 1945 (Public Law 1945, chapter 49, page 115) and 1956 (Public Law, chapter 61) now enshrined as New Jersey Statute 18A:65-1 et seq.</span></li>

       <li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note: Rutgers is the only one of the original nine <a href="/wiki/Colonial_colleges" title="Colonial colleges" class="mw-redirect">colonial colleges</a> to satisfy all three categories.
